    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_2672858647" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2672858647" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2672858647?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780606021791" href="/book/show/1423869.Summer_of_Fear">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2672858647" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16035418487358395622">Summer of fear by Lois Duncan is a 1977 publication. <br/><br/>This story is geared towards a young adult audience, but it still has some excellent chills and thrills even now, reading it as an adult. <br/><br/>For fans of trivia or pop culture, there was a made for television movie based on this book starring Linda Blair, which aired in 1978. However, I think the original title of the movie was ‘A Stranger in the House’. (It now shares the same title as the book and can be found easily on YouTube. Check it out, if</span>
  <span id="freeText16035418487358395622" style="display:none">Summer of fear by Lois Duncan is a 1977 publication. <br /><br />This story is geared towards a young adult audience, but it still has some excellent chills and thrills even now, reading it as an adult. <br /><br />For fans of trivia or pop culture, there was a made for television movie based on this book starring Linda Blair, which aired in 1978. However, I think the original title of the movie was ‘A Stranger in the House’. (It now shares the same title as the book and can be found easily on YouTube. Check it out, if for no other reason than to see a very young Fran Drescher)<br /><br />When Rachel’s aunt and uncle were killed in a fiery car crash, their orphaned daughter, Julia, comes to live with them. Soon, this shy, plain girl seems to have charmed every male in her general vicinity, included Rachel’s brother, her boyfriend, and even her father. <br /><br />Rachel begins to suspect Julia may be involved in the occult, but when she tries to convince her family, her warnings fall on deaf ears. Meanwhile, one by one, anyone who threatens Julia will suffer the consequences. <br /><br />A review for this book popped up on my Goodreads feed the other day and reminded me that I have a copy of this book stuffed somewhere on my own personal version of ‘the stacks’. Finding it felt like a chore I wasn’t sure I was ready to tackle, but I found it without having to dismantle my bookshelves entirely. It was fun to read this book again, even though the suspense doesn’t pack the same punch it did back in the seventies. <br /><br />However, it is still effective, especially for fans of psychological thrillers. However, I understand this book was reissued at some point with updates and revisions adding current technology into the story. I have not read the newer version, but based on the review I read recently, I would suggest hopping on over to eBay and finding a used copy of the older version and skip the updated version. <br />This is a short, nostalgic read, perfect for fans of YA with paranormal and psychological elements. <br />3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="16035418487358395622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Joe Valdez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez"><img alt="Joe Valdez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585885999p2/26876584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1729541432?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe Valdez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe Valdez" href="/user/show/26876584-joe-valdez">Joe Valdez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316099073" href="/book/show/9947386-summer-of-fear">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=paranormal-psychics">paranormal-psychics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26876584-joe-valdez?shelf=paranormal-general">paranormal-general</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1729541432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer188546812013723689">My Lois Duncan jag concludes with <i>Summer of Fear</i>, a supernatural thriller first published in 1976 and revised by the author in 2011 to account for changes in communication that would deflate much of her plot if the story took place in the present. I'm not wild about the trend to update Young Adult thrillers published in the 1970s or '80s for readers of today. Duncan's books are scarier when her teenage heroines can't rely on smartphones, the Internet or helicopter parents to help them overcome e</span>
  <span id="freeText188546812013723689" style="display:none">My Lois Duncan jag concludes with <i>Summer of Fear</i>, a supernatural thriller first published in 1976 and revised by the author in 2011 to account for changes in communication that would deflate much of her plot if the story took place in the present. I'm not wild about the trend to update Young Adult thrillers published in the 1970s or '80s for readers of today. Duncan's books are scarier when her teenage heroines can't rely on smartphones, the Internet or helicopter parents to help them overcome evil. In the '70s, you were on your own (think of Jamie Lee Curtis' babysitter character in <i>Halloween</i>). That said, Duncan knows how to craft a taut tale of primal fear and unsettle the reader regardless of the era.<br /><br />The story is the account of Rachel Bryant, a nineteen year old troubled by a newspaper article of a family who disappeared on a hiking trip. Rachel has questions about who could've photographed the family before their hike and whether this person of interest could be someone she knows. Moving back in time to the summer of Rachel's sweet sixteen birthday, the Bryants are a family of five living in suburban Albuquerque. Rachel's father Tom is a government engineer and her mother Leslie is a freelance photographer. Her older brother Peter is eighteen and plays bass in a rock band. Her younger brother Bobby is eleven and a pest. Rachel's dog Trickle rounds out the loving household.<br /><br />Set for a summer of repose, Rachel awakens to the news that her mother's sister Marge has been killed in a car accident near her Ozark Mountains home in Lost Ridge, Missouri with her husband and housekeeper. Rachel's Uncle Ryan was a novelist whose work kept Marge isolated and Rachel never met her surviving seventeen year old cousin, whose name is Julia Grant. While her parents are dispatched to the Ozarks to bring Julia home to live with them, Rachel discusses her apprehensions with Mike Gallagher, a childhood friend and lifeguard who has become something more than a friend. Rachel remains uncertain about sharing her room with a complete stranger.<br /><br /><i>Julia. It was a pretty name. I tried to remember the things I'd heard about Julia over the years. I knew, of course, that she went to a boarding school in New England because there were no good public schools in the area of her mountain home. I had a feeling she was supposed to have a talent of some kind. What was it she did--sing? Paint? Write poetry? To tell the truth, I had never been interested enough to make note of it, or of anything else from the dull family chitchat in Aunt Marge's annual Christmas letters. But now I did want to know. I wanted to prepare myself.</i><br /><br />Meeting her cousin for the first time, Rachel detects a dialect that awkwardly transitions from hillbilly to proper English and clothes that don't quite seem right for her. Julia peppers Rachel with questions about the family while shying away from answering many about herself. Meeting Trickle, Julia reacts with hostility to dogs and the feeling seems to be mutual. The next day, Rachel introduces her cousin to her friend Carolyn and the girls go shopping. Rachel is struck by how instantly taken Carolyn is with Julia. This phenomenon extends to her parents and even to her shy older brother Peter, who is positively googly-eyed over his first cousin. Impervious to Julia's charms is their neighbor Professor Jarvis, a retired professor of sociology at the University of New Mexico. <br /><br />Strange things are afoot in the Bryant household. When Trickle sinks his teeth into Julia's ankle, Rachel's father demands the family dog be leashed and kept outside; the poor mutt's health deteriorates quickly which Rachel's parents blame on an illness of some sort. Rachel comes across an article in her father's <i>National Geographic</i> about witchcraft, but dismisses it. In lieu of a summer dance, Rachel makes herself a dress, puzzling at why she chose pink, a color she dislikes and would look much better on a girl like ... Julia. Rachel wakes the morning of the dance stricken with hives and asks Mike to take Julia, letting her cousin borrow her new pink dress.<br /><br />Home alone, Rachel finds discarded matches in her bedroom and suspecting that her cousin might have a stash of cigarettes or marijuana nearby, rifles through the room. She discovers a waxlike sculpture shaped like a dog she can't make anything out of. Peter returns from the dance despondent and reports to his sister that Julia spent the night chatting with Mike. When Rachel confronts her boyfriend about this, he admits that he fell in love with Julia and hopes he and Rachel can still be friends. Cursing her cousin under her breath as a witch, Rachel goes for a chat with Professor Jarvis, who happened to just return from lecturing a women's club about witchcraft. <br /><br /><i>"We know that the mind has powers that often go undeveloped. Scientific tests conducted in laboratories have proved that certain people have more control over their mind forces than others. There are people who can predict the turn of a card or tune their minds in on events that are occurring in other places. Why then is it unreasonable to believe that there might be other people who can channel this mind force outward and create happenings instead of just know about them?"<br /><br />"And people who can do that are witches?"<br /><br />"Some of them call themselves that."</i><br /><br /><i>Summer of Fear</i> is not a great novel. The other titles I've read by Duncan (<i>I Know What You Did Last Summer</i>, <i>Down a Dark Hall</i>, <i>Daughters of Eve</i>, <i>The Third Eye</i>) are not great novels and I've gone on record here about how I feel about the special editions. Duncan struggles to suspend disbelief not because her books deal with psychic phenomena or criminal conspiracies among teenagers, but because the psychic phenomena and teenagers tend to be developed in the most generic and sanitized terms that qualify them for placement in the Young Adult category. On many levels, the characters think like adolescents might imagine adults think.<br /><br />Duncan is a much better writer than her rudimentary prose suggests and with this novel in particular, plugs into the sort of existential dread that a reader of nearly any age should be able to relate to. The fear that a charismatic individual no one else wants to see for what they are might take over and destroy your life is primal and exploited between the lines here beautifully. Every strange event that Rachel experiences is glossed over with a rational explanation by her parents and escalates another one of Duncan's themes: adults refuse to take teenagers seriously and want to control them. There isn't a wasted character or prop; every element Duncan introduces pays off by her climax, which on the page, are as exciting and unexpected as those favored by Alfred Hitchcock.<br /><br />Lois Duncan's work laid a foundation for the high school horror revival in American film in the mid-1990s, beginning with <i>Scream</i>. Wes Craven directed and twenty years earlier he directed the most faithful adaptation of Duncan's work with <i>Stranger in Our House</i>, a made-for-TV version of this novel that premiered on NBC on October 31, 1978. Linda Blair played Rachel, Lee Purcell played Julia and Fran Drescher played Carolyn (each of these actresses co-starred in an iconic movie of the '70s: <i>The Exorcist</i>, <i>Big Wednesday</i> and <i>Saturday Night Fever</i>. The Craven movie isn't remembered so fondly). The tiny perfection of Duncan's novels is that they table graphic depictions of violence and even profanity and are able to generate dread and unease with suggestion.</span>
  <a data-text-id="188546812013723689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1572806612" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1572806612" />
    <a title="Manybooks" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks"><img alt="Manybooks" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459773375p2/2970379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1572806612?book_show_action=true">Aug 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Manybooks" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Manybooks" href="/user/show/2970379-manybooks">Manybooks</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/18684284-summer-of-fear">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=childrens-literature">childrens-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2970379-manybooks?shelf=book-reviews">book-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1572806612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11706466022953724415">While yes, I did mildly enjoy Lois Duncan's 1976 young adult horror novel <u>Summer of Fear</u> when I read it as a teenager in 1982, revisiting <u>Summer of Fear</u> as an older adult has not at all been even remotely either a pleasurable or a rewarding reading experience for me. For sorry, but <u>Summer of Fear</u> is really so blatantly predictable that you not only are more than aware without even the shadow of a doubt right from square one that ALL of Rachel Bryant's fears with regard to her orphaned cousin Jul</span>
  <span id="freeText11706466022953724415" style="display:none">While yes, I did mildly enjoy Lois Duncan's 1976 young adult horror novel <u>Summer of Fear</u> when I read it as a teenager in 1982, revisiting <u>Summer of Fear</u> as an older adult has not at all been even remotely either a pleasurable or a rewarding reading experience for me. For sorry, but <u>Summer of Fear</u> is really so blatantly predictable that you not only are more than aware without even the shadow of a doubt right from square one that ALL of Rachel Bryant's fears with regard to her orphaned cousin Julia are one hundred percent justified and true (that Juila is an imposter and later turns out to be an an actual and bona fide witch), but also that while I found Rachel a positive and generally likeable character when I read <u>Sumer of Fear</u> as a teenager, rereading the novel now rather shows her as in many ways a bratty and nastily opinionated individual. <br /><br />And while of course it is fake cousin Julia/Sarah who turns out to be the witch-like main villain of <u>Summer of Fear</u>, personally, I have been almost feeling a wee bit sorry for her this time around, as not only does Rachel from the very beginning act extremely negatively towards her supposed cousin, the author's, Lois Duncan's attitude towards the inhabitants of the Ozark Mountains of Missouri has indeed also made me personally very much annoyed and uncomfortable (because truly and in my opinion, Duncan with her text, with her narrative and especially with the main villain of <u>Summer of Fear</u>, seems to continuously insinuate and claim that if the established, the original long-term inhabitants of the Ozark Mountains are not uncouth, uneducated, superstitious hillbilly types, they are cold and calculating witches like Julia/Sarah who will even resort to murder and mayhem in order to obtain and keep their desires). So therefore, even though I do have to admit that <u>Summer of Fear</u> is well enough written and as a teenager, certainly kept me up all night reading with suspense and appreciation, I really can and will now only grant a one star ranking at best for <u>Summer of Fear</u> (and yes, <u>Summer of Fear</u> is thus also and sadly most definitely a novel that I actively regret having revisited, for what was mildly entertaining, suspenseful and readable in 1982 has now completely dissipated, and really, Lois Duncan's obvious authorial and personal disdain for the people of the Ozark Mountains of Missouri does majorly make me cringe and rub me the wrong proverbial way).</span>
  <a data-text-id="11706466022953724415" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Bren" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61659069-bren"><img alt="Bren" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590193281p2/61659069.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1913383220?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bren" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bren" href="/user/show/61659069-bren">Bren</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=dark-and-heavy">dark-and-heavy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=read-and-reviewed">read-and-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=thriller-horror">thriller-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=better-or-worse-than-expected">better-or-worse-than-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/61659069-bren?shelf=young-adult-mystery">young-adult-mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1913383220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14245279129577396659">"It's been four years now since that summer. It's still with me. Maybe it always will be."<br/>Summer of Fear <br/>by Lois Duncan<br/><br/><br/><br/>This is one creepy story and it is perfect to read in the summer, particularly if you want something that will make your skin crawl.<br/><br/>For a YA mystery, Summer of Fear is genuinely scary and a bit haunting. Of all Duncan's books this maybe the scariest.<br/><br/>It is also one that I rated fairly low. Why?<br/><br/>Because I simply could not STAND the villain. I mean I had such issues with her I reall</span>
  <span id="freeText14245279129577396659" style="display:none">"It's been four years now since that summer. It's still with me. Maybe it always will be."<br />Summer of Fear <br />by Lois Duncan<br /><br /><br /><br />This is one creepy story and it is perfect to read in the summer, particularly if you want something that will make your skin crawl.<br /><br />For a YA mystery, Summer of Fear is genuinely scary and a bit haunting. Of all Duncan's books this maybe the scariest.<br /><br />It is also one that I rated fairly low. Why?<br /><br />Because I simply could not STAND the villain. I mean I had such issues with her I really..I mean it was just so hard to read about her. I wanted to punch her and that isn't a good thing.<br /><br />I will warn you there is ANIMAL CRUELTY in this book which is another reason it gets such a low rating from me. I love Duncan. I grew up with her books. This one is a no from me but it isn't because it's not a good read. It is to creepy, I hate animal deaths in books and the villainess made me want to smack her.<br /><br />This is YA. Rachel and her parents are horrified when they hear that the parents of Rachel's cousin Julia have died in a car wreck. This leaves Julia with no family and so Rachel's family takes her in.<br /><br />Rachel is excited. Julia is her age and Rachel figures they can be friends. That is..until she meets Julia..<br /><br />Julia is like nobody Rachel has ever met. She is mysterious and very creepy. Rachel can easily see this. So why does everyone else think Julia is such an amazing person...<br /><br />Do not underestimate the creepy factor in this one. It's there. But it is not my favorite by Duncan but that is because of the reasons I mentioned above. In fact I so disliked Julia, it prevented me from really enjoying this book. That has not happened with many of Duncan's books.<br /><br />SPOILERS:<br /><br /><br />I can't help it. Through the book, everyone turns on Rachel and it does not help that there is a brutal animal death in this book so I would automatically take points off for that. I hate that writers so often use this plot devise.<br /><br /> I did do a reread to see if I liked it any better in adulthood and I do not.<br /><br />The bottom line is Duncan is probably my favorite YA author but this one gets a hard pass from me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14245279129577396659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer1877144496275092772"><i>Summer of Fear</i> is a short, simple read that I enjoyed but that I didn't find special. Part of the issue is that I read this as an adult rather than as a young adult, so the "fear factor" and mystery did not really hit me. Aside from this, the book was predictable and, though I did not predict everything exactly, I definitely saw one or two things coming. I didn't really grow connected to any of the characters, unfortunately. Nonetheless, if you are looking for a quick read that will bring back s</span>
  <span id="freeText1877144496275092772" style="display:none"><i>Summer of Fear</i> is a short, simple read that I enjoyed but that I didn't find special. Part of the issue is that I read this as an adult rather than as a young adult, so the "fear factor" and mystery did not really hit me. Aside from this, the book was predictable and, though I did not predict everything exactly, I definitely saw one or two things coming. I didn't really grow connected to any of the characters, unfortunately. Nonetheless, if you are looking for a quick read that will bring back some nostalgia, this could be a solid choice.</span>

<div id="review_858998772" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858998772" />
    <a title="ElphaReads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876063-elphareads"><img alt="ElphaReads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1410383933p2/4876063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/858998772?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ElphaReads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ElphaReads" href="/user/show/4876063-elphareads">ElphaReads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876063-elphareads?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876063-elphareads?shelf=thrillers-adventure-and-suspense">thrillers-adventure-and-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876063-elphareads?shelf=reading-list-2014">reading-list-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer858998772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5846679635035765613">Have you ever felt overshadowed by a prettier, more popular relative? Maybe a sibling, or a cousin? Someone who you think is just the worst person in the world, but everyone seems to love and make excuses for? And no matter how much you protest, that person is always held in highest regard, and YOU'RE the hysterical and mean one?<br/><br/>Have you considered that perhaps your relative is a practicing witch? Because Lois Duncan sure has!<br/><br/>Rachel lives a fairly good life in Albuquerque. She's close to her par</span>
  <span id="freeText5846679635035765613" style="display:none">Have you ever felt overshadowed by a prettier, more popular relative? Maybe a sibling, or a cousin? Someone who you think is just the worst person in the world, but everyone seems to love and make excuses for? And no matter how much you protest, that person is always held in highest regard, and YOU'RE the hysterical and mean one?<br><br>Have you considered that perhaps your relative is a practicing witch? Because Lois Duncan sure has!<br><br>Rachel lives a fairly good life in Albuquerque. She's close to her parents, has a couple of pretty nice brothers named Peter and Bobby, a friendly dog, a fun best friend named Carolyn and a wonderful boyfriend named Mike. Summer has just started, and she's expecting it to be a good one. Unfortunately, her family gets the news that her aunt and uncle on her mother's side were killed in a terrible car crash in the Ozarks, leaving behind her cousin Julia. Julia, with no where else to go, is taken in by Rachel's family. They've never actually met Julia before, as the aunt and uncle lived a very solitary life due to the uncle's pretentious 'I'm a writer I need peace and quiet!' lifestyle. So meeting Julia is kind of scary for Rachel. While her family takes to her right away, Rachel thinks that something is very wrong with her cousin. The dog, Trickle, immediately dislikes her. And everyone starts to favor Julia. Mother starts to treat her like her only daughter. Peter seems to fall in love with her (this seemed a bit George Michael Bluth to me!). Dad is also quite taken. And soon, Julia has stolen both Carolyn and Mike from Rachel, becoming a new girlfriend, a new best friend. Rachel knows that something is very wrong, and when she finds a burning wax figure in teh room they share together, things go from bad, to much much worse.<br><br>Now, I get that there were extenuating circumstances here, in that Julia was a witch who was literally bewitching everyone. But my GOD, Rachel's parents are the worst parents ever. The frustration I felt for them was limitless, as even when Julia wasn't around (and it was implied that the power over them wasn't as great) they just had no interest in listening to THEIR OWN DAUGHTER at all. Granted, Rachel wasn't exactly the best player of the game of thrones (girl, don't act hysterical and accuse the girl of witchcraft willy nilly!), but she's their DAUGHTER for God's sake. Like, I would hope that if I said 'hey mom and dad, my cousin definitely stole my boyfriend', they would say 'well that's really awful of her, maybe we should all talk about this' instead of 'well boys fall in and out of love so fast and it's not Julia's fault that she's so pretty'. Cripes. But it was definitely the biggest frustration that Rachel went about this all wrong. You don't want to sound like the hysterical one, Rachel. Like, ever.<br><br>The book was a bit dated. It wasn't explicitly dated until the Mom said she had gone on a double date with Elizabeth Montgomery of BEWITCHED fame, and suddenly everyone was wearing Paisley and bell bottoms in my mind. It did build up a nice amount of suspense though, as I was tearing through the last ten pages to see what happened. I had a feeling that it would all work out relatively okay (Duncan's endings tend to do that for the most part), but I was still racing on through. Just in case it took a KILLING MR. GRIFFIN turn. Witchcraft and bitchcraft abound, SUMMER OF FEAR was a quick read and would definitely have been right up my teenage alley, what with my love for the FEAR STREET novels and all that. <br><br>Also, fun fact, Linda Blair starred as Rachel in a made for TV adaptation back in the 70s.<br><br><a href="http://s164.photobucket.com/user/elphabachan/media/reviewnongifs/lysummer_zps29e7cc49.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1392909437i/8631737.png" alt=" photo lysummer_zps29e7cc49.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>If that doesn't date this, I don't know what does.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5846679635035765613" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1509869267" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1509869267" />
    <a title="Abraham Nava" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46844301-abraham-nava"><img alt="Abraham Nava" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441982085p2/46844301.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1509869267?book_show_action=true">Jan 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abraham Nava" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abraham Nava" href="/user/show/46844301-abraham-nava">Abraham Nava</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1509869267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer515998756551945603"> Do you like books about magic spells or witchcraft well this is the right book for you! The genre to this book is fantasy fiction with a little bit of realistic fiction. My opinion to this book is that it is great it is creepy in a way and makes you feel like you are actually there in the experience. There will be SPOILER ALERTS in the book so be aware.<br/> So this book takes place in day and night in a house of this girl named Rachel. So what happens in this book is that what suddenly tragic just </span>
  <span id="freeText515998756551945603" style="display:none"> Do you like books about magic spells or witchcraft well this is the right book for you! The genre to this book is fantasy fiction with a little bit of realistic fiction. My opinion to this book is that it is great it is creepy in a way and makes you feel like you are actually there in the experience. There will be SPOILER ALERTS in the book so be aware.<br /> So this book takes place in day and night in a house of this girl named Rachel. So what happens in this book is that what suddenly tragic just happened to the family is that Rachel's aunt and uncle just got killed in a car accident and their daughter named Julia needed to stay with a new family. And the family is Rachel's because there is no where else for her to stay with. What Rachel notices of Julia is that she is a little strange. She has a strange personality that Rachel is curious about. And as time passed on strange things started happening Rachel's dog died and her neighbor was in a coma sort of thing. What Rachel later knows is that Julia was the one who caused all of this and is a witch who wants to marry her father and kill anything that gets in her way. The conflict is person vs. person since it is Rachel vs evil witch JULIA. I think a major theme in the story is when Julia proves she is a WITCH.<br /> The setting in the story adds to the end of the story because when Julia told Rachel that her mother will die when she hits the curve in the mountain Rachel hurries to the mountain to stop her mother from passing away and does save her. I think the author really did bring tension when Rachel and her ex boyfriend raced towards the highway to prevent her mother from falling to her death in the curve. Another thing the author used to bring tension was when the car had a gas leak and had to run toward the mountain but still made it.<br /> I was very satisfied the way the author brought tension in the book, I really enjoy this author Louis Duncan because of how he always gets me hooked up in the book. I get so tense that I completely zone out on whats happening around me. I was surprised when I found out that little sweet Julia was actually a EVIL WITCH. I thought to myself that it can't be possible that a nice girl like her is evil.<br /> I rate this book a 4 because I think Lois Duncan could've added more to the book because I felt like he could've added more to the book. So if you like books about crazy witches or something dramatic or fantasy fiction read THIS BOOK NOW.</span>
  <a data-text-id="515998756551945603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_725307431" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/725307431" />
    <a title="Eden" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2263713-eden"><img alt="Eden" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564182083p2/2263713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/725307431?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Eden" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Eden" href="/user/show/2263713-eden">Eden</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2263713-eden?shelf=50-states-challenge">50-states-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2263713-eden?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2263713-eden?shelf=books-to-buy">books-to-buy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer725307431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5418858684560802907">Rachel is fifteen, has a great boyfriend and a great family. But one day they get horrible news: Rachel's mother's sister and her husband were killed in a car accident. Their daughter, Julia, is now all alone. But Rachel's mother and father get ready to go get their niece. They hardly know her, but she is family. And Rachel is fine with this. Sure, it will take some getting used to sharing her room with someone, but it will be like having an older sister.<br/><br/>Everything was going well. At least for a</span>
  <span id="freeText5418858684560802907" style="display:none">Rachel is fifteen, has a great boyfriend and a great family. But one day they get horrible news: Rachel's mother's sister and her husband were killed in a car accident. Their daughter, Julia, is now all alone. But Rachel's mother and father get ready to go get their niece. They hardly know her, but she is family. And Rachel is fine with this. Sure, it will take some getting used to sharing her room with someone, but it will be like having an older sister.<br /><br />Everything was going well. At least for a little bit, until Julia showed Rachel her true colors. The problem is, no one else seems to see the true Julia but Rachel and she's not sure how to convince anyone that her cousin is not the angel she pretends to be. <br /><br />I know I stayed up later last night reading this than I should have, but I honestly couldn't put it down. It was definitely a page-turner and at the same time, so frustrating! Honestly, I felt very angry at times because of everything Rachel went through and no one believed her. <br /><br />The story was suspenseful and kept me on the edge of my seat (or, uh, bed, rather). I wasn't really sure what was going to happen next and I worried for Rachel's safety. And her family and boyfriend just annoyed me because of the fact they couldn't see what was going on. Julia was always the victim and Rachel always the bad guy, the one they must punish.<br /><br /><br />What else can I say about this book? It was great, even if some of the characters frustrated me to no end. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5418858684560802907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/677730699?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rayne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rayne" href="/user/show/5374178-rayne">Rayne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316099073" href="/book/show/9947386-summer-of-fear">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=witches-and-wizards">witches-and-wizards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=there-s-romance-in-there-somewhere">there-s-romance-in-there-somewhere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=between-3-and-4-stars">between-3-and-4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5374178-rayne?shelf=totally-saw-that-coming">totally-saw-that-coming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer677730699" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1332959918056043766"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>In terms of the atmosphere in the novel and the general enjoyment that I got from this story, this should probably get a bit more than 3 stars. I am well aware that this is an oldie and that I am probably not in the target audience of this book any more, but I was a bit disappointed by it. I found it way to simple and a bit too predictable, but I did enjoy reading it, aside from that jerk of a love interest and Rae's parents, who had no problem calling their own daughter a witch, pointi</span>
  <span id="freeText1332959918056043766" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />In terms of the atmosphere in the novel and the general enjoyment that I got from this story, this should probably get a bit more than 3 stars. I am well aware that this is an oldie and that I am probably not in the target audience of this book any more, but I was a bit disappointed by it. I found it way to simple and a bit too predictable, but I did enjoy reading it, aside from that jerk of a love interest and Rae's parents, who had no problem calling their own daughter a witch, pointing out her faults in comparison to her cousin and not protesting when people her brothers called her a bitch in front of everyone. All in all, this was a quick, somewhat creepy, fun and easy read. I think I will be checking out Duncan's other titles. </span>

<div id="review_2490177589" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_96497195" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/96497195" />
    <a title="Steph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2142019-steph"><img alt="Steph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604524058p2/2142019.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/96497195?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph" href="/user/show/2142019-steph">Steph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142019-steph?shelf=stand-alone">stand-alone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142019-steph?shelf=year-read-2010">year-read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142019-steph?shelf=author-%EC%9B%83">author-웃</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142019-steph?shelf=age-group-ya-na">age-group-ya-na</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2142019-steph?shelf=audiobook-listened-to">audiobook-listened-to</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer96497195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3413691356580017755"><b>
  <i>Summer of Fear</i>
</b> was written in 1976 for young adults and has won several book awards: <br/>California Young Reader Medal for Vermont Young Readers Award, Vermont Young Readers Award and the New Mexico Young Readers Award. I chose to read this book for my "Lifetime of Books" challenge. If I hadn't had that challenge, I'm certain I never would've read this book. That being said, it was an entertaining read. I borrowed the audio version from the library and, although the narrator's voice didn't fit, </span>
  <span id="freeText3413691356580017755" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Summer of Fear</i>
</b> was written in 1976 for young adults and has won several book awards: <br />California Young Reader Medal for Vermont Young Readers Award, Vermont Young Readers Award and the New Mexico Young Readers Award. I chose to read this book for my "Lifetime of Books" challenge. If I hadn't had that challenge, I'm certain I never would've read this book. That being said, it was an entertaining read. I borrowed the audio version from the library and, although the narrator's voice didn't fit, IMO, the book was easy to listen to.<br /><br />Rachel is a 17 year old girl living with her two brothers and her parents in Albuquerque, NM. She's dating the boy next door and ready to enjoy the summer. But, one day the family receives devastating news, Rachel's aunt and uncle have been killed in a car crash leaving her cousin, Julia all alone. Her parents decide to have Julia live with them. When they return with Julia, Rachel is determined to make a good impression and help her feel at home with her family. <br /><br />Julia is not what she expected though. She's quiet, has "piercing eyes" and "talks funny". Julia and her family were living in the Ozark Mtns while her father wrote a novel. <br /><br />Rachel starts to notice very odd things about Julia. She tries hard to get her family and friends to see them too, but they begin to think that Rachel's just jealous of all the attention her cousin is getting.<br /><br />The story moved quickly and soon the readers find themselves rooting for Rachel and her plans to expose Julia for what she really is. It was interesting reading a story that was written 34 years ago. I enjoyed it more than I thought I would.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3413691356580017755" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/468434989?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luke Sewell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luke Sewell" href="/user/show/12966036-luke-sewell">Luke Sewell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer468434989" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer837451393168216744"><br/> <br/> The book Summer if Fear by Louis Duncan, in my eyes was one of the best books that I had ever read. The book is about a teenager named Rachel who had been looking forward to summer all year an when it finally arrives is overjoyed. She has a loving family, an amazing best friend, and the best boyfriend that a boy could ask for. All of they changed though when she came. When her family learned that their aunt and uncle had died they decided to adopt their cousin into their lives. This would be t</span>
  <span id="freeText837451393168216744" style="display:none"><br /> <br /> The book Summer if Fear by Louis Duncan, in my eyes was one of the best books that I had ever read. The book is about a teenager named Rachel who had been looking forward to summer all year an when it finally arrives is overjoyed. She has a loving family, an amazing best friend, and the best boyfriend that a boy could ask for. All of they changed though when she came. When her family learned that their aunt and uncle had died they decided to adopt their cousin into their lives. This would be the downfall of Rachel's summer. When the girl arrived nothing was out of the normal and everything was fine, but then weird things started to occur an Rachel knew that her cousin Julia was the cause. Rachel's stubbornness drove away everyone she cared about but in the end they would all know she was right.<br /> This book really was one of the best books that I have ever read. It was one of those books that captivated me to the point where I couldn't put it down and was reading it all the time. The mystery within the story was really the thing that kept everything going. You always fin out little things about Julia and that Rachel is right but it's never enough to satisfy your wanting for Julia to be evil. The way that Louis Duncan portrayed all of the characters was also amazing. He made Julia humble at first but then grow into the villain that everyone wants, and Rachel is the hero that despite nobody believes he she always gets up and tries again. This book was amazing in every way and I would recommend it to anyone looking to read a good book</span>
  <a data-text-id="837451393168216744" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5537592548310371239">My 12 year old self is so happy I decided to reread this Lois Duncan novel. Oh my heart of hearts. When I read that first page I was immediately thrown back to the long, hot summers of my middle school years. <br/><br/>I couldn’t believe I actually remembered the plot and the characters. It’s been 35 plus years since I originally read this book. And let me say, I loved it just as much now as I did then. Rereading this was wonderful. I didn’t realize it was the modernized version of the book, however I hav</span>
  <span id="freeText5537592548310371239" style="display:none">My 12 year old self is so happy I decided to reread this Lois Duncan novel. Oh my heart of hearts. When I read that first page I was immediately thrown back to the long, hot summers of my middle school years. <br /><br />I couldn’t believe I actually remembered the plot and the characters. It’s been 35 plus years since I originally read this book. And let me say, I loved it just as much now as I did then. Rereading this was wonderful. I didn’t realize it was the modernized version of the book, however I have no problem with that since Duncan did the update. I’m hoping to pass it on to my daughters. <br /><br />I would definitely recommend this book, as well as all her other books, to a middle grade reader. Scary, weird and just the right amount of romance! Still my favorite formula for a good novel at 50.</span>

<div id="review_175003299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/175003299" />
    <a title="Carolina Dean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5596902-carolina-dean"><img alt="Carolina Dean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589045181p2/5596902.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/175003299?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolina Dean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolina Dean" href="/user/show/5596902-carolina-dean">Carolina Dean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175003299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17458164730761823918">Summer of Fear is one of several stories written by noted author Lois Duncan (I Know What You Did Last Summer, Hotel for Dogs) famous for her young adult novels. It is told in the first-person from the perspective of Rachael, a teenage girl living an idyllic life in Albuquerque, New Mexico in the late 1970's. <br/><br/>Rachael enjoys a loving, close-knit family (including two brothers), a best friend, and a dog named Trickle. Despite her hangups about her curly red hair, Rachael also has a cute boyfriend </span>
  <span id="freeText17458164730761823918" style="display:none">Summer of Fear is one of several stories written by noted author Lois Duncan (I Know What You Did Last Summer, Hotel for Dogs) famous for her young adult novels. It is told in the first-person from the perspective of Rachael, a teenage girl living an idyllic life in Albuquerque, New Mexico in the late 1970's. <br /><br />Rachael enjoys a loving, close-knit family (including two brothers), a best friend, and a dog named Trickle. Despite her hangups about her curly red hair, Rachael also has a cute boyfriend named Mike, who is literally the-boy-next-door. <br /><br />Things begin to change for Rachael when her older cousin Julie comes to live with her family after Julie's parents are killed in a car accident in the Ozarks where they had been living. Whereas before Rachael enjoyed being the only young female in the household, she now has to learn to share everything with her cousin, including her clothes, her bedroom, and her friends. At first, Rachael and Julie get along well but Rachael slowly begins to notice strange things about her cousin. First, her southern accent inexplicably comes and goes and then Trickle, who had always been a gentle dog, takes a strong dislike to Julie to the point of biting her which results in his banishment from the house.<br /><br />As Julie becomes more outgoing, Rachael draws into herself straining her relationships with her family, her best friend, and even her boyfriend Mike, who takes more than a liking to Julie. When it seems that Julie is going to take everything away from her, Rachael investigates her cousin further and finds some surprising inconsistencies as well as evidence that Julie may be practicing black-magic on her, her family, and her loved ones. As the mystery unfolds, Rachel discovers Julie's horrific plan for her and her family. <br /><br />There really isn't a lot to not like about this book. The characters were all believable and I really felt that the author captured the feel of the late 1970's (which was actually the present when Summer of Fear was written.) The plot was mysterious enough to hold one's interest, although the observant reader will figure out the twist way ahead of Rachael. I liked that the mythology of the story drew upon real-life beliefs and practices found along the Appalachian Trial and that Rachael alluded to the works of Vance Randolph in her research, although it is not explicitly stated. At just over 200 pages, Summer of Fear is a quick read perfect for whiling away a lazy summer day.<br /><br />Like some of Duncan's other novels before, Summer of Fear was renamed Stranger In Our House and made into a film in 1978 directed by Wes Craven and starring Linda Blair as Rachael and, a then unknown, Fran Drescher as Rachael's best friend. Stranger in Our House first aired on Halloween night in 1978 and later aired regularly on TBS along with other 70's occult movies such as The Spell (1977). In 2003, it was made available on both VHS and DVD. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17458164730761823918" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The main characters is Rachael, Julie Rachel's parents and Mike. This story talks about a girl named Rachel that seems to have a perfect life her parents love her and has a best friend oh and she has her boyfriend named Mike how is the boy next boor so her neighbor and has a dog named trickles and 2 brothers. Rachel was really looking forward to the summer. while Rachel seems to have it all her cosines parents die in a car crash so her uncles Rachel's parents decided to take care of her witch ruined Rachel summer because Julie comes to live with her and now she is not the only girl and she liked being the only yong girl in the house and not just that but she had to share the same room cloths and even friends too thin she starts to realize weird things like her dog turned really man to Julie to the point that he bit Julie. thin she divorced that Julie practiced black magic and wanted to take everything away from Rachel and wanted too kill her parents but at the end they catch her and everything was finally over. I think this book is person vs person because is Rachael fighting with her cosine Julie that ends up being a witch. <br /><br /> A major events that changes the main character was that at the beginning of the story she had everything and her life was going just perfect until her cosine came into her life and slowly took everything away from her and wanted to destroy it. I think this way she changed from the beginning of the story because maybe know she can appreciate more what she has and all she went through trying to help her mom of death mad her really strong than she was at the beginning of the story.<br /><br /> The part i was surprised in was when we all finally discover who Julie really was. It was really nice seeing it all go down on Julie. I like the end when all the problem is solved in the book it stats The summer of fear lies well behind us. I really liked the how it all finally came to a end and everyone of the book was happy even me. <br /><br /> I rate this book a 5 stars. i give it this rate because it had all i really like in a book fear suspension and creepy events. I recommend this book to how ever likes to get scared and likes creepy things and surprises. This book us full of surprises and creepy event if you like these type of books i would really recommend u to read this.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17352967158307586599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_857284398" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/857284398" />
    <a title="Halcyon Daze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5783023-halcyon-daze"><img alt="Halcyon Daze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386238990p2/5783023.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/857284398?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Halcyon Daze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Halcyon Daze" href="/user/show/5783023-halcyon-daze">Halcyon Daze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5783023-halcyon-daze?shelf=two-star">two-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5783023-halcyon-daze?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5783023-halcyon-daze?shelf=lois-duncan">lois-duncan</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5783023-halcyon-daze?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857284398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6857452738892808081">I didn't like this book. At first, I didn't understand why. I mean, it isn't too fundamentally different from Duncan's other books, which I typically enjoy.<br/><br/>It was boring.<br/><br/>Our main character is typical American teenager Rachel, who's living the good life. She gets along with her family, she has a boyfriend whom she loves, she's well-liked, etc. One day, her cousin Julia is orphaned and brought in to live with them. Strange things begin to happen, and Julia slowly begins to take away Rachel's frien</span>
  <span id="freeText6857452738892808081" style="display:none">I didn't like this book. At first, I didn't understand why. I mean, it isn't too fundamentally different from Duncan's other books, which I typically enjoy.<br /><br />It was boring.<br /><br />Our main character is typical American teenager Rachel, who's living the good life. She gets along with her family, she has a boyfriend whom she loves, she's well-liked, etc. One day, her cousin Julia is orphaned and brought in to live with them. Strange things begin to happen, and Julia slowly begins to take away Rachel's friends, boyfriends, and family love for herself.<br /><br />It's a sound concept, but I didn't particularly like the way it was written. Nothing particularly exciting happened until the end. Julia would do something like cozy up to Rachel's boyfriend. Rachel would get jealous and suspect something's up. Rachel would discover some strange item in the trash. Rachel complains to her parents, who basically ignore her. Rinse and repeat.<br /><br />Another thing was that I didn't find our main character very interesting. I mean, she was written to be Ordinary Teenage Girl, so her personality fell rather flat. She likes doing teenage stuff like shopping for swimsuits. She likes her boyfriend. And so forth. Again, she wasn't bad or offensive - just very boring.<br /><br />In fact, I found the character of Julia to be way more interesting, particularly the twist at the end. I wish the story was more about her and less about Rachel.<br /><br />Incidentally, I found something very hard to believe. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Julia turns out not to be Julia at all, but as someone masquerading as her. The real Julia's been dead the whole time. While the reveal is rather creepy and well-written, it really falls apart. I mean, nobody asked for proper documentation of any sort? Or asked about her background and realized that two and two didn't add up to four? I mean, she was supposedly an orphaned minor being sent to live with relatives. In this book, she basically just moves in with a suitcase. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="6857452738892808081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1313830975" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1313830975" />
    <a title="Dana Berglund" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/177678-dana-berglund"><img alt="Dana Berglund" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1184121497p2/177678.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1313830975?book_show_action=true">Jun 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Berglund" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Berglund" href="/user/show/177678-dana-berglund">Dana Berglund</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/177678-dana-berglund?shelf=youngadult">youngadult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1313830975" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14116823473324518165">I inhaled Lois Duncan's books as an adolescent. They felt dangerous, and sometimes mind-blowing (like the one about astral projection, for example!) without being the gore-fest of horror books intended for adults. I felt older, wiser, cooler, and harder for having read them. I decided to revisit one as part of my reading goals for this year. I wasn't aware when I checked it out that Summer of Fear was part of a rerelease of a number of Duncan's books, with edits for the modern reader. I don't th</span>
  <span id="freeText14116823473324518165" style="display:none">I inhaled Lois Duncan's books as an adolescent. They felt dangerous, and sometimes mind-blowing (like the one about astral projection, for example!) without being the gore-fest of horror books intended for adults. I felt older, wiser, cooler, and harder for having read them. I decided to revisit one as part of my reading goals for this year. I wasn't aware when I checked it out that Summer of Fear was part of a rerelease of a number of Duncan's books, with edits for the modern reader. I don't think these edits are a bad idea, as I do feel that casual reader teens have a hard time really getting into the setting of a book with landlines and roller skates. In this case, however, the edits didn't mesh seamlessly, and they felt incomplete. I can accept the explanation of the mother's old school photography- I can. But there are still landlines, and handwritten letters from school friends, with no email or Internet research. Furthermore, the girls go to the mall together to shop for.... fabric and dress patterns to make their own dresses for the upcoming dance! This is not an activity that most teenagers today would identify with. I never even made my own dress to a dance. (Digression: it turned out that making doll clothes was too hard. I watched my mom make clothes for me instead.) Who advised Duncan and let her haphazardly edit some of the era's markers, but not all?<br />The story still holds some power. Rachel has a great teenage girl-movie life, until a tragedy brings her cousin (who she's never met) to live with them. And Julia is clearly up to no good, but no one will listen to Rachel! (Think Single While Female.) Frustrations of not being heard, not trusting others, feeling alone....it all still works, I think.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14116823473324518165" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('A4+/f/aCS0Z+EIWy/n150TKw4K0EydZCIF3TyYnc1G8SjGKzTXVfyrc82NAk+oHxxsnJ74sMQHrBGXz6Zx9zKw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wY3nYyYWABFcakwjtprNiAaX5QEl3D544+Z8+Kjt7DTQjjqvneEUnZVGEUFsHTWo8u7MQ6oZqEACotPLRi5LcA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan">About Lois Duncan</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/26819.Lois_Duncan"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1197061058p3/26819.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11665544816017740172">Lois Duncan (born Lois Duncan Steinmetz) was an American writer and novelist, known primarily for her books for children and young adults, in particular (and some times controversially considering her young readership) crime thrillers. Duncan's parents were the noted magazine photographers Lois Steinmetz and Joseph Janney Steinmetz. She was born in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, but grew up in Saraso</span>
  <span id="freeText11665544816017740172" style="display:none">Lois Duncan (born Lois Duncan Steinmetz) was an American writer and novelist, known primarily for her books for children and young adults, in particular (and some times controversially considering her young readership) crime thrillers. Duncan's parents were the noted magazine photographers Lois Steinmetz and Joseph Janney Steinmetz. She was born in Philadelphia, Pennsylvania, but grew up in Sarasota, Florida. Duncan started writing and submitting manuscripts to magazines at the age of ten, and when she was thirteen succeeded in selling her first story.<br /><br />Duncan attended Duke University from 1952 to 1953 but dropped out, married, and started a family. During this time, she continued to write and publish magazine articles; over the course of her career, she has published more than 300 articles, in magazines such as Ladies' Home Journal, Redbook, McCall's, Good Housekeeping, and Reader's Digest. After her first marriage, which produced three children, ended in divorce, Duncan moved to Albuquerque, New Mexico, to teach journalism at the University of New Mexico, where she also earned a BA in English in 1977. In 1965 she married Don Arquette, and had two more children with him.<br /><br />Duncan was best known for her novels of suspense for teenagers. Some of her works have been adapted for the screen, the most famous example being the 1997 film I Know What You Did Last Summer, adapted from her novel of the same title. Other made-for-TV movies include Stranger with My Face, Killing Mr. Griffin, Don't Look Behind You, Summer of Fear and Gallows Hill.<br /><br />In 1989 the youngest of Duncan's children, Kaitlyn Arquette, was murdered in Albuquerque, New Mexico, under suspicious circumstances. Who Killed My Daughter? relates the facts and conjecture about the still unsolved case. <br /><br />Duncan's second book about her daughter's murder, ONE TO THE WOLVES: ON THE TRAIL OF A KILLER, picks up where the first book leaves off and contains all the new information Kait's family has uncovered from private investigation. <br /><br />The 1971 children's book Hotel for Dogs was released as a theatrical movie in 2009, starring Emma Roberts. That book has now been republished by Scholastic along with two sequels, News for Dogs (2009) and Movie for Dogs (2010).<br /><br />Duncan's Gothic suspense novel, DOWN A DARK HALL, is being filmed for the Big Screen and will probably be released in 2016.<br /><br /><br />Follow Lois on Twitter: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://twitter.com/duncanauthor">http://twitter.com/duncanauthor</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=100000216477747&amp;ref=profile">http://www.facebook.com/profile.php?i...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.kaitarquette.arquettes.com">http://www.kaitarquette.arquettes.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11665544816017740172" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
